```
def Vect.zipWith.match_1.{u_1, u_2, u_3} : {α : Type u_1} →
  {β : Type u_2} →
    (motive : (x : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) → Vect α x → Vect β x → Sort u_3) →
      (x : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) →
        (x_1 : Vect α x) →
          (x_2 : Vect β x) →
            ([Unit](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/The-Unit-Type/#Unit "Documentation for Unit in Lean Language Reference") → motive 0 nil nil) →
              ((n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) →
                  (a : α) → (as : Vect α n) → (b : β) → (bs : Vect β n) → motive n.[succ](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ in Lean Language Reference") (cons a as) (cons b bs)) →
                motive x x_1 x_2 :=
fun {α} {β} motive x x_1 x_2 h_1 h_2 =>
  Nat.casesOn (motive := fun x => (x_3 : Vect α x) → (x_4 : Vect β x) → motive x x_3 x_4) x
    (fun x x_3 =>
      casesOn (motive := fun a x_4 => [Nat.zero](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.zero in Lean Language Reference") [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") a → x [≍](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#HEq___refl "Documentation for HEq in Lean Language Reference") x_4 → motive [Nat.zero](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.zero in Lean Language Reference") x x_3) x
        (fun h h_3 =>
          ⋯ ▸
            casesOn (motive := fun a x => [Nat.zero](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.zero in Lean Language Reference") [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") a → x_3 [≍](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#HEq___refl "Documentation for HEq in Lean Language Reference") x → motive [Nat.zero](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.zero in Lean Language Reference") nil x_3) x_3
              (fun h h_4 => ⋯ ▸ h_1 [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/The-Unit-Type/#Unit___unit "Documentation for Unit.unit in Lean Language Reference")[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/The-Unit-Type/#Unit___unit "Documentation for Unit.unit in Lean Language Reference")) (fun a {n} a_1 h => [False.elim](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Truth/#False___elim "Documentation for False.elim in Lean Language Reference") ⋯) ⋯ ⋯)
        (fun a {n} a_1 h => [False.elim](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Truth/#False___elim "Documentation for False.elim in Lean Language Reference") ⋯) ⋯ ⋯)
    (fun n x x_3 =>
      casesOn (motive := fun a x_4 => n.[succ](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ in Lean Language Reference") [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") a → x [≍](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#HEq___refl "Documentation for HEq in Lean Language Reference") x_4 → motive n.[succ](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ in Lean Language Reference") x x_3) x (fun h => [False.elim](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Truth/#False___elim "Documentation for False.elim in Lean Language Reference") ⋯)
        (fun a {n_1} a_1 h =>
          n.elimOffset n_1 1 h fun x_4 =>
            Eq.ndrec (motive := fun {n_2} => (a_2 : Vect α n_2) → x [≍](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#HEq___refl "Documentation for HEq in Lean Language Reference") cons a a_2 → motive n.[succ](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ in Lean Language Reference") x x_3)
              (fun a_2 h =>
                ⋯ ▸
                  casesOn (motive := fun a_3 x => n.[succ](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ in Lean Language Reference") [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") a_3 → x_3 [≍](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#HEq___refl "Documentation for HEq in Lean Language Reference") x → motive n.[succ](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ in Lean Language Reference") (cons a a_2) x_3) x_3
                    (fun h => [False.elim](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Truth/#False___elim "Documentation for False.elim in Lean Language Reference") ⋯)
                    (fun a_3 {n_2} a_4 h =>
                      n.elimOffset n_2 1 h fun x =>
                        Eq.ndrec (motive := fun {n_3} =>
                          (a_5 : Vect β n_3) → x_3 [≍](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#HEq___refl "Documentation for HEq in Lean Language Reference") cons a_3 a_5 → motive n.[succ](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ in Lean Language Reference") (cons a a_2) x_3)
                          (fun a_5 h => ⋯ ▸ h_2 n a a_2 a_3 a_5) x a_4)
                    ⋯ ⋯)
              x_4 a_1)
        ⋯ ⋯)
    x_1 x_2
```

`end Vect `
The `zipWith` function is even more tedious to define by hand than the `tail` function. We encourage you to try it, using `Vect.recOn`, `Vect.casesOn` and `Vect.noConfusion`.
##  8.9. Inaccessible Patterns[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=inaccessible-patterns "Permalink")
Sometimes an argument in a dependent matching pattern is not essential to the definition, but nonetheless has to be included to specialize the type of the expression appropriately. Lean allows users to mark such subterms as _inaccessible_ for pattern matching. These annotations are essential, for example, when a term occurring in the left-hand side is neither a variable nor a constructor application, because these are not suitable targets for pattern matching. We can view such inaccessible patterns as “don't care” components of the patterns. You can declare a subterm inaccessible by writing `.(t)`. If the inaccessible pattern can be inferred, you can also write `_`.
The following example, we declare an inductive type that defines the property of “being in the image of `f`”. You can view an element of the type `[ImageOf](Induction-and-Recursion/#ImageOf "Definition of example") f b` as evidence that `b` is in the image of `f`, whereby the constructor `imf` is used to build such evidence. We can then define any function `f` with an “inverse” which takes anything in the image of `f` to an element that is mapped to it. The typing rules forces us to write `f a` for the first argument, but this term is neither a variable nor a constructor application, and plays no role in the pattern-matching definition. To define the function `inverse` below, we _have to_ mark `f a` inaccessible.
`inductive ImageOf {α β : Type u} (f : α → β) : β → Type u where   | imf : (a : α) → [ImageOf](Induction-and-Recursion/#ImageOf "Definition of example") f (f a)  ``[open](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Namespaces-and-Sections/#Lean___Parser___Command___open "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") ImageOf  ``def inverse {f : α → β} : (b : β) → [ImageOf](Induction-and-Recursion/#ImageOf "Definition of example") f b → α   | .(f a), [imf](Induction-and-Recursion/#ImageOf "Definition of example") a => a  ``def inverse' {f : α → β} : (b : β) → [ImageOf](Induction-and-Recursion/#ImageOf "Definition of example") f b → α   | _, [imf](Induction-and-Recursion/#ImageOf "Definition of example") a => a ```
In the example above, the inaccessible annotation makes it clear that `f` is _not_ a pattern matching variable.
Inaccessible patterns can be used to clarify and control definitions that make use of dependent pattern matching. Consider the following definition of the function `Vect.add`, which adds two vectors of elements of a type, assuming that type has an associated addition function:
`inductive Vect (α : Type u) : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → Type u   | nil  : Vect α 0   | cons : α → {n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")} → Vect α n → Vect α (n+1)  ``def Vect.add [[Add](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Add___mk "Documentation for Add in Lean Language Reference") α] : {n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")} → Vect α n → Vect α n → Vect α n   | 0,   nil,       nil       => nil   | `unused variable `n`  Note: This linter can be disabled with `set_option linter.unusedVariables false``n+1, cons a as, cons b bs => cons (a + b) (add as bs) ```
The argument `{n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")}` appear after the colon, because it cannot be held fixed throughout the definition. When implementing this definition, the equation compiler starts with a case distinction as to whether the first argument is `0` or of the form `n+1`. This is followed by nested case splits on the next two arguments, and in each case the equation compiler rules out the cases are not compatible with the first pattern.
But, in fact, a case split is not required on the first argument; the `casesOn` eliminator for `Vect` automatically abstracts this argument and replaces it by `0` and `n + 1` when we do a case split on the second argument. Using inaccessible patterns, we can prompt the equation compiler to avoid the case split on `n`.
`inductive Vect (α : Type u) : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → Type u   | nil  : Vect α 0   | cons : α → {n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")} → Vect α n → Vect α (n+1) [namespace](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Namespaces-and-Sections/#Lean___Parser___Command___namespace "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") Vect `
`def add [[Add](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Add___mk "Documentation for Add in Lean Language Reference") α] : {n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")} → Vect α n → Vect α n → Vect α n   | .(_), nil,       nil       => nil   | .(_), cons a as, cons b bs => cons (a + b) (add as bs) `
`end Vect `
Marking the position as an inaccessible pattern tells the equation compiler first, that the form of the argument should be inferred from the constraints posed by the other arguments, and, second, that the first argument should _not_ participate in pattern matching.
The inaccessible pattern `.(_)` can be written as `_` for convenience.
`inductive Vect (α : Type u) : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → Type u   | nil  : Vect α 0   | cons : α → {n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")} → Vect α n → Vect α (n+1) [namespace](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Namespaces-and-Sections/#Lean___Parser___Command___namespace "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") Vect `
`def add [[Add](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Add___mk "Documentation for Add in Lean Language Reference") α] : {n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")} → Vect α n → Vect α n → Vect α n   | _, nil,       nil       => nil   | _, cons a as, cons b bs => cons (a + b) (add as bs) `
`end Vect `
As we mentioned above, the argument `{n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")}` is part of the pattern matching, because it cannot be held fixed throughout the definition. Rather than requiring that these discriminants be provided explicitly, Lean implicitly includes these extra discriminants automatically for us.
`inductive Vect (α : Type u) : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → Type u   | nil  : Vect α 0   | cons : α → {n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")} → Vect α n → Vect α (n+1) [namespace](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Namespaces-and-Sections/#Lean___Parser___Command___namespace "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") Vect `
`def add [[Add](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Add___mk "Documentation for Add in Lean Language Reference") α] {n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")} : Vect α n → Vect α n → Vect α n   | nil,       nil       => nil   | cons a as, cons b bs => cons (a + b) (add as bs) `
`end Vect `
When combined with the _auto bound implicits_ feature, you can simplify the declare further and write:
`inductive Vect (α : Type u) : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → Type u   | nil  : Vect α 0   | cons : α → {n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")} → Vect α n → Vect α (n+1) [namespace](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Namespaces-and-Sections/#Lean___Parser___Command___namespace "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") Vect `
`def add [[Add](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Add___mk "Documentation for Add in Lean Language Reference") α] : Vect α n → Vect α n → Vect α n   | nil,       nil       => nil   | cons a as, cons b bs => cons (a + b) (add as bs) `
`end Vect `
Using these new features, you can write the other vector functions defined in the previous sections more compactly as follows:
`set_option linter.unusedVariables false inductive Vect (α : Type u) : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → Type u   | nil  : Vect α 0   | cons : α → {n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")} → Vect α n → Vect α (n+1) [namespace](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Namespaces-and-Sections/#Lean___Parser___Command___namespace "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") Vect `
`def head : Vect α (n+1) → α   | cons a as => a  ``def tail : Vect α (n+1) → Vect α n   | cons a as => as  ``theorem eta : (v : Vect α (n+1)) → cons (head v) (tail v) = v   | cons a as => [rfl](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#rfl-next "Documentation for rfl in Lean Language Reference")  ``def map (f : α → β → γ) : Vect α n → Vect β n → Vect γ n   | nil,       nil       => nil   | cons a as, cons b bs => cons (f a b) (map f as bs)  ``def zip : Vect α n → Vect β n → Vect (α × β) n   | nil,       nil       => nil   | cons a as, cons b bs => cons (a, b) (zip as bs) `
`end Vect `
##  8.10. Match Expressions[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=match-expressions "Permalink")
Lean also provides a compiler for `match`-`with` expressions found in many functional languages:
`set_option linter.unusedVariables false `
`def isNotZero (m : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) : [Bool](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool in Lean Language Reference") :=   [match](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") m [with](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")   | 0     => [false](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.false in Lean Language Reference")   | n + 1 => [true](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.true in Lean Language Reference") ```
This does not look very different from an ordinary pattern matching definition, but the point is that a `match` can be used anywhere in an expression, and with arbitrary arguments.
`set_option linter.unusedVariables false `
`def isNotZero (m : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) : [Bool](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool in Lean Language Reference") :=   [match](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") m [with](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")   | 0     => [false](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.false in Lean Language Reference")   | n + 1 => [true](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.true in Lean Language Reference")  ``def filter (p : α → [Bool](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool in Lean Language Reference")) : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") α → [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") α   | []      => []   | a :: as =>     [match](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") p a [with](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")     | [true](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.true in Lean Language Reference") => a :: [filter](Induction-and-Recursion/#isNotZero-next "Definition of example") p as     | [false](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.false in Lean Language Reference") => [filter](Induction-and-Recursion/#isNotZero-next "Definition of example") p as  ``example : [filter](Induction-and-Recursion/#isNotZero-next "Definition of example") isNotZero [1, 0, 0, 3, 0] = [1, 3] := rfl ```
Here is another example:
`def foo (n : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) (b c : [Bool](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool in Lean Language Reference")) :=   5 + [match](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") n - 5, b && c [with](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")       | 0,     [true](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.true in Lean Language Reference")  => 0       | m + 1, [true](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.true in Lean Language Reference")  => m + 7       | 0,     [false](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.false in Lean Language Reference") => 5       | m + 1, [false](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.false in Lean Language Reference") => m + 3  ```9`[#eval](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Interacting-with-Lean/#Lean___Parser___Command___eval "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") foo 7 [true](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.true in Lean Language Reference") [false](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.false in Lean Language Reference")`
```
9
```
` ``example : foo 7 [true](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.true in Lean Language Reference") [false](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.false in Lean Language Reference") = 9 := rfl ```
Lean uses the `match` construct internally to implement pattern-matching in all parts of the system. Thus, all four of these definitions have the same net effect:
`def bar₁ : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") × [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")   | (m, n) => m + n  ``def bar₂ (p : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") × [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") :=   [match](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") p [with](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")   | (m, n) => m + n  ``def bar₃ : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") × [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") :=   fun (m, n) => m + n  ``def bar₄ (p : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") × [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") :=   let (m, n) := p; m + n ```
These variations are equally useful for destructing propositions:
`[variable](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Namespaces-and-Sections/#Lean___Parser___Command___variable "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") (p q : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → Prop)  ``example : (∃ x, p x) → (∃ y, q y) → ∃ x y, p x ∧ q y   | ⟨x, px⟩, ⟨y, qy⟩ => ⟨x, y, px, qy⟩  ``example (h₀ : ∃ x, p x) (h₁ : ∃ y, q y)         : ∃ x y, p x ∧ q y :=   [match](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") h₀, h₁ [with](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")   | ⟨x, px⟩, ⟨y, qy⟩ => ⟨x, y, px, qy⟩  ``example : (∃ x, p x) → (∃ y, q y) → ∃ x y, p x ∧ q y :=   fun ⟨x, px⟩ ⟨y, qy⟩ => ⟨x, y, px, qy⟩  ``example (h₀ : ∃ x, p x) (h₁ : ∃ y, q y)         : ∃ x y, p x ∧ q y :=   let ⟨x, px⟩ := h₀   let ⟨y, qy⟩ := h₁   ⟨x, y, px, qy⟩ ```
##  8.11. Exercises
  1. Open a namespace `Hidden` to avoid naming conflicts, and use the equation compiler to define addition, multiplication, and exponentiation on the natural numbers. Then use the equation compiler to derive some of their basic properties.
  2. Similarly, use the equation compiler to define some basic operations on lists (like the `[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference")` function) and prove theorems about lists by induction (such as the fact that `[reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") ([reverse](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse in Lean Language Reference") xs) = xs` for any list `xs`).
  3. Define your own function to carry out course-of-value recursion on the natural numbers. Similarly, see if you can figure out how to define `[WellFounded.fix](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFounded___fix "Documentation for WellFounded.fix in Lean Language Reference")` on your own.
  4. Following the examples in the section on [dependent pattern matching](Induction-and-Recursion/#dependent-pattern-matching), define a function that will append two vectors. This is tricky; you will have to define an auxiliary function.
  5. Consider the following type of arithmetic expressions. The idea is that `var`` ``n` is a variable, `vₙ`, and `const`` ``n` is the constant whose value is `n`.
`inductive Expr where   | const : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example")   | var : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example")   | plus : [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example")   | times : [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") deriving [Repr](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Interacting-with-Lean/#Repr___mk "Documentation for Repr in Lean Language Reference")  ``[open](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Namespaces-and-Sections/#Lean___Parser___Command___open "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") Expr  ``def sampleExpr : [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") :=   [plus](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") ([times](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") ([var](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") 0) ([const](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") 7)) ([times](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") ([const](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") 2) ([var](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") 1)) ```
Here `sampleExpr` represents `(v₀ * 7) + (2 * v₁)`.
Write a function that evaluates such an expression, evaluating each `[var](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") n` to `v n`.
`inductive Expr where   | const : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example")   | var : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example")   | plus : [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example")   | times : [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example")   deriving [Repr](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Interacting-with-Lean/#Repr___mk "Documentation for Repr in Lean Language Reference") [open](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Namespaces-and-Sections/#Lean___Parser___Command___open "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") Expr def sampleExpr : [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") :=   [plus](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") ([times](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") ([var](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") 0) ([const](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") 7)) ([times](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") ([const](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") 2) ([var](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") 1)) `
`def `declaration uses 'sorry'`eval (v : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) : [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") | [const](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") n => sorry | [var](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") n => v n | [plus](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") e₁ e₂ => sorry | [times](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") e₁ e₂ => sorry ``def sampleVal : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")   | 0 => 5   | 1 => 6   | _ => 0  ``-- Try it out. You should get 47 here. -- #eval eval sampleVal sampleExpr `
Implement “constant fusion,” a procedure that simplifies subterms like `5 + 7` to `12`. Using the auxiliary function `simpConst`, define a function “fuse”: to simplify a plus or a times, first simplify the arguments recursively, and then apply `simpConst` to try to simplify the result.
`inductive Expr where   | const : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example")   | var : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example")   | plus : [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example")   | times : [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example")   deriving [Repr](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Interacting-with-Lean/#Repr___mk "Documentation for Repr in Lean Language Reference") [open](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Namespaces-and-Sections/#Lean___Parser___Command___open "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") Expr def `declaration uses 'sorry'`eval (v : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) : [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") | [const](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") n => sorry | [var](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") n => v n | [plus](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") e₁ e₂ => sorry | [times](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") e₁ e₂ => sorry `
`def simpConst : [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example")   | [plus](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") ([const](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") n₁) ([const](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") n₂)  => [const](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") (n₁ + n₂)   | [times](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") ([const](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") n₁) ([const](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") n₂) => [const](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") (n₁ * n₂)   | e                           => e  ``def `declaration uses 'sorry'`fuse : [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") → [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example") := sorry ``theorem `declaration uses 'sorry'`simpConst_eq (v : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) : ∀ e : [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example"), [eval](Induction-and-Recursion/#eval "Definition of example") v ([simpConst](Induction-and-Recursion/#simpConst "Definition of example") e) = [eval](Induction-and-Recursion/#eval "Definition of example") v e := sorry ``theorem `declaration uses 'sorry'`fuse_eq (v : [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference") → [Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")) : ∀ e : [Expr](Induction-and-Recursion/#Expr "Definition of example"), [eval](Induction-and-Recursion/#eval "Definition of example") v ([fuse](Induction-and-Recursion/#simpConst "Definition of example") e) = [eval](Induction-and-Recursion/#eval "Definition of example") v e := sorry ```
The last two theorems show that the definitions preserve the value.
